In my view, 2000 is very different from 2020, and much has changed – in particular, three big obstacles are in the way. First of all, while China no longer sees Vietnam as being that important in terms of socialist solidarity, Vietnam still needs this solidarity in its parrying of democratisation attempts by the US. Since the late 1980s, China has declared to Vietnam that their bilateral relationship is not special and no different from China’s relationship with its other neighbours."}]},{"type":"newsletter"},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","data":"It is doubtful the mutual consultations among the communist parties on their experience with socialism and of their mutual grievances will have any impact on Chinese foreign policy towards Vietnam – particularly in terms of cutting back the Chinese push in the South China Sea, which Vietnam full-heartedly hates. Mutual suspicions fester, and their economic ties are not as strong as they can be. As has happened in the past, Vietnam is just a subplot of China’s efforts to barricade its southern flank against Western encroachment. China’s larger aims are to achieve its core interests and to be on good terms with the US or Russia.
